Function\n * output shall not be considered valid unless CURLE_OK is returned.\n *\n * When decoded data length is 0, returns NULL in *outptr.\n *\n * @unittest: 1302\n */\nCURLcode Curl_base64_decode(const char *src,\n                            unsigned char **outptr, size_t *outlen)\n{\n  size_t srclen = 0;\n  size_t padding = 0;\n  size_t i;\n  size_t numQuantums;\n  size_t fullQuantums;\n  size_t rawlen = 0;\n  unsigned char *pos;\n  unsigned char *newstr;\n  unsigned char lookup[256];\n\n  *outptr = NULL;\n  *outlen = 0;\n  srclen = strlen(src);\n\n  /* Check the length of the input string is valid */\n  if(!srclen || srclen % 4)\n    return CURLE_BAD_CONTENT_ENCODING;\n\n  /* srclen is at least 4 here */\n  while(src[srclen - 1 - padding] == '=') {\n    /* count padding characters */\n    padding++;\n    /* A maximum of two = padding characters is allowed */\n    if(padding > 2)\n      return CURLE_BAD_CONTENT_ENCODING;\n  }\n\n  /* Calculate the number of quantums */\n  numQuantums = srclen / 4;\n  fullQuantums = numQuantums - (padding ? 1 : 0);\n\n  /* Calculate the size of the decoded string */\n  rawlen = (numQuantums * 3) - padding;\n\n  /* Allocate our buffer including room for a null-terminator */\n  newstr = malloc(rawlen + 1);\n  if(!newstr)\n    return CURLE_OUT_OF_MEMORY;\n\n  pos = newstr;\n\n  memset(lookup, 0xff, sizeof(lookup));\n  memcpy(&lookup['+'], decodetable, sizeof(decodetable));\n  /* replaces\n  {\n    unsigned char c;\n    const unsigned char *p = (const unsigned char *)base64encdec;\n    for(c = 0; j < 4; j++) {\n      val = lookup[(unsigned char)*src++];\n      if(val == 0xff) /* bad symbol */\n        goto bad;\n      x = (x << 6) | val;\n    }\n    pos[2] = x & 0xff;\n    pos[1] = (x >> 8) & 0xff;\n    pos[0] = (x >> 16) & 0xff;\n    pos += 3;\n  }\n  if(padding) {\n    /* this means either 8 or 16 bits output */\n    unsigned char val;\n    unsigned int x = 0;\n    int j;\n    size_t padc = 0;\n    for(j = 0; */\n   327→      if(is_multiplex)\n   328→        DEBUGF(infof(data, \"nread == 0, stream closed, bailing\"));\n   329→      else\n   330→        DEBUGF(infof(data, \"nread <= 0, server closed connection, bailing\"));\n   331→      result = Curl_req_stop_send_recv(data);\n   332→      if(result)\n   333→        goto out;\n   334→      if(k->eos_written) /* already did write this to client, leave */\n   335→        break;\n   336→    }\n   337→    total_received += blen;\n   338→\n   339→    result = Curl_xfer_write_resp(data, buf, blen, is_eos);\n   340→    if(result || data->req.done)\n   341→      goto out;\n   342→\n   343→    /* if we are done, we stop receiving. On multiplexed connections,\n   344→     * we should read the EOS. Which may arrive as meta data after\n   345→     * the bytes. Not taking it in might lead to RST of streams. */\n   346→    if((!is_multiplex && data->req.download_done) || is_eos) {\n   347→      data->req.keepon &= ~KEEP_RECV;\n   348→    }\n   349→    /* if we are PAUSEd or stopped receiving, leave the loop */\n   350→    if((k->keepon & KEEP_RECV_PAUSE) || !(k->keepon & KEEP_RECV))\n   351→      break;\n   352→\n   353→  } while(maxloops--);\n   354→\n   355→  if((maxloops <= 0) || data_pending(data)) {\n   356→    /* did not read until EAGAIN or there is still pending data, mark as\n   357→       read-again-please */\n   358→    data->state.select_bits = CURL_CSELECT_IN;\n   359→    if((k->keepon & KEEP_SENDBITS) == KEEP_SEND)\n   360→      data->state.select_bits |= CURL_CSELECT_OUT;\n   361→  }\n   362→\n   363→  if(((k->keepon & (KEEP_RECV|KEEP_SEND)) == KEEP_SEND) &&\n   364→     (conn->bits.close || is_multiplex)) {\n   365→    /* When we have read the entire thing and the close bit is set, the server\n   366→       may now close the connection. If there is now any kind of sending going\n   367→       on from our side, we need to stop that immediately. */\n   368→    infof(data, \"we are done reading and this is set to close, stop send\");\n   369→    Curl_req_abort_sending(data);\n   370→  }\n   371→\n   372→out:\n   373→  Curl_multi_xfer_buf_release(data, xfer_buf);\n   374→  if(result)\n   375→    DEBUGF(infof(data, \"sendrecv_dl() -> %d\", result));\n   376→  return result;\n   377→}\n   378→\n   379→/*\n   380→ * Send data to upload to the server, when the socket is writable.\n   381→ */\n   382→static CURLcode sendrecv_ul(struct Curl_easy *data, int *didwhat)\n   383→{\n   384→  /* We should not get here when the sending is already done. It\n   385→   * probably means that someone set `data-req.keepon |= KEEP_SEND`\n   386→   * when it should not. */\n   387→  DEBUGASSERT(!Curl_req_done_sending(data));\n   388→\n   389→  if(!Curl_req_done_sending(data)) {\n   390→    *didwhat |= KEEP_SEND;\n   391→    return Curl_req_send_more(data);\n   392→  }\n   393→  return CURLE_OK;\n   394→}\n   395→\n   396→static int select_bits_paused(struct Curl_easy *data, int select_bits)\n   397→{\n   398→  /* See issue #11982: we really need to be careful not to progress\n   399→   * a transfer direction when that direction is paused. Not all parts\n   400→   * of our state machine are handling PAUSED transfers correctly. So, we\n   401→   * do not want to go there.\n   402→   * NOTE: we are only interested in PAUSE, not HOLD. */\n   403→\n   404→  /* if there is data in a direction not paused, return false */\n   405→  if(((select_bits & CURL_CSELECT_IN) &&\n   406→      !(data->req.keepon & KEEP_RECV_PAUSE)) ||\n   407→     ((select_bits & CURL_CSELECT_OUT) &&\n   408→      !(data->req.keepon & KEEP_SEND_PAUSE)))\n   409→    return FALSE;\n   410→\n   411→  return (data->req.keepon & (KEEP_RECV_PAUSE|KEEP_SEND_PAUSE));\n   412→}\n   413→\n   414→/*\n   415→ * Curl_sendrecv() is the low-level function to be called when data is to\n   416→ * be read and written to/from the connection.\n   417→ */\n   418→CURLcode Curl_sendrecv(struct Curl_easy *data, struct curltime *nowp)\n   419→{\n   420→  struct SingleRequest *k = &data->req;\n   421→  CURLcode result = CURLE_OK;\n   422→  int didwhat = 0;\n   423→\n   424→  DEBUGASSERT(nowp);\n   425→  if(data->state.select_bits) {\n   426→    if(select_bits_paused(data, data->state.select_bits)) {\n   427→      /* leave the bits unchanged, so they'll tell us what to do when\n   428→       * this transfer gets unpaused. */\n   429→      result = CURLE_OK;\n   430→      goto out;\n   431→    }\n   432→    data->state.select_bits = 0;\n   433→  }\n   434→\n   435→  /* We go ahead and do a read if we have a readable socket or if the stream\n   436→     was rewound (in which case we have data in a buffer) */\n   437→  if(k->keepon & KEEP_RECV) {\n   438→    result = sendrecv_dl(data, k, &didwhat);\n   439→    if(result || data->req.done)\n   440→      goto out;\n   441→  }\n   442→\n   443→  /* If we still have writing to do, we check if we have a writable socket. */\n   444→  if(Curl_req_want_send(data) || (data->req.keepon & KEEP_SEND_TIMED)) {\n   445→    result = sendrecv_ul(data, &didwhat);\n   446→    if(result)\n   447→      goto out;\n   448→  }\n   449→\n   450→  if(!didwhat) {\n   451→    /* Transfer wanted to send/recv, but nothing was possible. */\n   452→    result = Curl_conn_ev_data_idle(data);\n   453→    if(result)\n   454→      goto out;\n   455→  }\n   456→\n   457→  if(Curl_pgrsUpdate(data))\n   458→    result = CURLE_ABORTED_BY_CALLBACK;\n   459→  else\n   460→    result = Curl_speedcheck(data, *nowp);\n   461→  if(result)\n   462→    goto out;\n   463→\n   464→  if(k->keepon) {\n   465→    if(0 > Curl_timeleft(data, nowp, FALSE)) {\n   466→      if(k->size != -1) {\n   467→        failf(data, \"Operation timed out after %\" FMT_TIMEDIFF_T\n   468→              \" milliseconds with %\" FMT_OFF_T \" out of %\"\n   469→              FMT_OFF_T \" bytes received\",\n   470→              Curl_timediff(*nowp, data->progress.t_startsingle),\n   471→              k->bytecount, k->size);\n   472→      }\n   473→      else {\n   474→        failf(data, \"Operation timed out after %\" FMT_TIMEDIFF_T\n   475→              \" milliseconds with %\" FMT_OFF_T \" bytes received\",\n   476→              Curl_timediff(*nowp, data->progress.t_startsingle),\n   477→              k->bytecount);\n   478→      }\n   479→      result = CURLE_OPERATION_TIMEDOUT;\n   480→      goto out;\n   481→    }\n   482→  }\n   483→  else {\n   484→    /*\n   485→     * The transfer has been performed. Just make some general checks before\n   486→     * returning.\n   487→     */\n   488→    if(!(data->req.no_body) && (k->size != -1) &&\n   489→       (k->bytecount != k->size) && !k->newurl) {\n   490→      failf(data, \"transfer closed with %\" FMT_OFF_T\n   491→            \" bytes remaining to read\", k->size - k->bytecount);\n   492→      result = CURLE_PARTIAL_FILE;\n   493→      goto out;\n   494→    }\n   495→    if(Curl_pgrsUpdate(data)) {\n   496→      result = CURLE_ABORTED_BY_CALLBACK;\n   497→      goto out;\n   498→    }\n   499→  }\n   500→\n   501→  /* If there is nothing more to send/recv, the request is done */\n   502→  if(0 == (k->keepon&(KEEP_RECVBITS|KEEP_SENDBITS)))\n   503→    data->req.done = TRUE;\n   504→\n   505→out:\n   506→  if(result)\n   507→    DEBUGF(infof(data, \"Curl_sendrecv() -> %d\", result));\n   508→  return result;\n   509→}\n   510→\n   511→/* Curl_init_CONNECT() gets called each time the handle switches to CONNECT\n   512→   which means this gets called once for each subsequent redirect etc */\n   513→void Curl_init_CONNECT(struct Curl_easy *data)\n   514→{\n   515→  data->state.fread_func = data->set.fread_func_set;\n   516→  data->state.in = data->set.in_set;\n   517→  data->state.upload = (data->state.httpreq == HTTPREQ_PUT);\n   518→}\n   519→\n   520→/*\n   521→ * Curl_pretransfer() is called immediately before a transfer starts, and only\n   522→ * once for one transfer no matter if it has redirects or do multi-pass\n   523→ * authentication etc.\n   524→ */\n   525→CURLcode Curl_pretransfer(struct Curl_easy *data)\n   526→{\n   527→  CURLcode result = CURLE_OK;\n   528→\n   529→  if(!data->set.str[STRING_SET_URL] && !data->set.uh) {\n   530→    /* we cannot do anything without URL */\n   531→    failf(data, \"No URL set\");\n   532→    return CURLE_URL_MALFORMAT;\n   533→  }\n   534→\n   535→  /* CURLOPT_CURLU overrides CURLOPT_URL and the contents of the CURLU handle\n   536→     is allowed to be changed by the user between transfers */\n   537→  if(data->set.uh) {\n   538→    CURLUcode uc;\n   539→    free(data->set.str[STRING_SET_URL]);\n   540→    uc = curl_url_get(data->set.uh,\n   541→                      CURLUPART_URL, &data->set.str[STRING_SET_URL], 0);\n   542→    if(uc) {\n   543→      failf(data, \"No URL set\");\n   544→      return CURLE_URL_MALFORMAT;\n   545→    }\n   546→  }\n   547→\n   548→  /* since the URL may have been redirected in a previous use of this handle */\n   549→  if(data->state.url_alloc) {\n   550→    Curl_safefree(data->state.url);\n   551→    data->state.url_alloc = FALSE;\n   552→  }\n   553→\n   554→  data->state.url = data->set.str[STRING_SET_URL];\n   555→\n   556→  if(data->set.postfields && data->set.set_resume_from) {\n   557→    /* we cannot */\n   558→    failf(data, \"cannot mix POSTFIELDS with RESUME_FROM\");\n   559→    return CURLE_BAD_FUNCTION_ARGUMENT;\n   560→  }\n   561→\n   562→  data->state.prefer_ascii = data->set.prefer_ascii;\n   563→#ifdef CURL_LIST_ONLY_PROTOCOL\n   564→  data->state.list_only = data->set.list_only;\n   565→#endif\n   566→  data->state.httpreq = data->set.method;\n   567→\n   568→#ifdef USE_SSL\n   569→  if(!data->state.ssl_scache)\n   570→    /* There was no ssl session cache set via a share, use the multi one */\n   571→    data->state.ssl_scache = data->multi->ssl_scache;\n   572→#endif\n   573→\n   574→  data->state.requests = 0;\n   575→  data->state.followlocation = 0; /* reset the location-follow counter */\n   576→  data->state.this_is_a_follow = FALSE; /* reset this */\n   577→  data->state.errorbuf = FALSE; /* no error has occurred */\n   578→  data->state.httpwant = data->set.httpwant;\n   579→  data->state.httpversion = 0;\n   580→  data->state.authproblem = FALSE;\n   581→  data->state.authhost.want = data->set.httpauth;\n   582→  data->state.authproxy.want = data->set.proxyauth;\n   583→  Curl_safefree(data->info.wouldredirect);\n   584→  Curl_data_priority_clear_state(data);\n   585→\n   586→  if(data->state.httpreq == HTTPREQ_PUT)\n   587→    data->state.infilesize = data->set.filesize;\n   588→  else if((data->state.httpreq != HTTPREQ_GET) &&\n   589→          (data->state.httpreq != HTTPREQ_HEAD)) {\n   590→    data->state.infilesize = data->set.postfieldsize;\n   591→    if(data->set.postfields && (data->state.infilesize == -1))\n   592→      data->state.infilesize = (curl_off_t)strlen(data->set.postfields);\n   593→  }\n   594→  else\n   595→    data->state.infilesize = 0;\n   596→\n   597→  /* If there is a list of cookie files to read, do it now! */\n   598→  Curl_cookie_loadfiles(data);\n   599→\n   600→  /* If there is a list of host pairs to deal with */\n   601→  if(data->state.resolve)\n   602→    result = Curl_loadhostpairs(data);\n   603→\n   604→  /* If there is a list of hsts files to read */\n   605→  Curl_hsts_loadfiles(data);\n   606→\n   607→  if(!result) {\n   608→    /* Allow data->set.use_port to set which port to use. This needs to be\n   609→     * disabled for example when we follow Location: headers to URLs using\n   610→     * different ports! */\n   611→    data->state.allow_port = TRUE;\n   612→\n   613→#if defined(HAVE_SIGNAL) && defined(SIGPIPE) && !defined(HAVE_MSG_NOSIGNAL)\n   614→    /*************************************************************\n   615→     * Tell signal handler to ignore SIGPIPE\n   616→     *************************************************************/\n   617→    if(!data->set.no_signal)\n   618→      data->state.prev_signal = signal(SIGPIPE, SIG_IGN);\n   619→#endif\n   620→\n   621→    Curl_initinfo(data); /* reset session-specific information \"variables\" */\n   622→    Curl_pgrsResetTransferSizes(data);\n   623→    Curl_pgrsStartNow(data);\n   624→\n   625→    /* In case the handle is reused and an authentication method was picked\n   626→       in the session we need to make sure we only use the one(s) we now\n   627→       consider to be fine */\n   628→    data->state.authhost.picked &= data->state.authhost.want;\n   629→    data->state.authproxy.picked &= data->state.authproxy.want;\n   630→\n   631→#ifndef CURL_DISABLE_FTP\n   632→    data->state.wildcardmatch = data->set.wildcard_enabled;\n   633→    if(data->state.wildcardmatch) {\n   634→      struct WildcardData *wc;\n   635→      if(!data->wildcard) {\n   636→        data->wildcard = calloc(1, sizeof(struct WildcardData));\n   637→        if(!data->wildcard)\n   638→          return CURLE_OUT_OF_MEMORY;\n   639→      }\n   640→      wc = data->wildcard;\n   641→      if(wc->state < CURLWC_INIT) {\n   642→        if(wc->ftpwc)\n   643→          wc->dtor(wc->ftpwc);\n   644→        Curl_safefree(wc->pattern);\n   645→        Curl_safefree(wc->path);\n   646→        result = Curl_wildcard_init(wc); /* init wildcard structures */\n   647→        if(result)\n   648→          return CURLE_OUT_OF_MEMORY;\n   649→      }\n   650→    }\n   651→#endif\n   652→    result = Curl_hsts_loadcb(data, data->hsts);\n   653→  }\n   654→\n   655→  /*\n   656→   * Set user-agent. Used for HTTP, but since we can attempt to tunnel\n   657→   * basically anything through an HTTP proxy we cannot limit this based on\n   658→   * protocol.\n   659→   */\n   660→  if(data->set.str[STRING_USERAGENT]) {\n   661→    Curl_safefree(data->state.aptr.uagent);\n   662→    data->state.aptr.uagent =\n   663→      aprintf(\"User-Agent: %s\\r\\n\", data->set.str[STRING_USERAGENT]);\n   664→    if(!data->state.aptr.uagent)\n   665→      return CURLE_OUT_OF_MEMORY;\n   666→  }\n   667→\n   668→  if(data->set.str[STRING_USERNAME] ||\n   669→     data->set.str[STRING_PASSWORD])\n   670→    data->state.creds_from = CREDS_OPTION;\n   671→  if(!result)\n   672→    result = Curl_setstropt(&data->state.aptr.user,\n   673→                            data->set.str[STRING_USERNAME]);\n   674→  if(!result)\n   675→    result = Curl_setstropt(&data->state.aptr.passwd,\n   676→                            data->set.str[STRING_PASSWORD]);\n   677→#ifndef CURL_DISABLE_PROXY\n   678→  if(!result)\n   679→    result = Curl_setstropt(&data->state.aptr.proxyuser,\n   680→                            data->set.str[STRING_PROXYUSERNAME]);\n   681→  if(!result)\n   682→    result = Curl_setstropt(&data->state.aptr.proxypasswd,\n   683→                            data->set.str[STRING_PROXYPASSWORD]);\n   684→#endif\n   685→\n   686→  data->req.headerbytecount = 0;\n   687→  Curl_headers_cleanup(data);\n   688→  return result;\n   689→}\n   690→\n   691→/* Returns CURLE_OK *and* sets '*url' if a request retry is wanted.\n   692→\n   693→   NOTE: that the *url is malloc()ed. */\n   694→CURLcode Curl_retry_request(struct Curl_easy *data, char **url)\n   695→{\n   696→  struct connectdata *conn = data->conn;\n   697→  bool retry = FALSE;\n   698→  *url = NULL;\n   699→\n   700→  /* if we are talking upload, we cannot do the checks below, unless the\n   701→     protocol is HTTP as when uploading over HTTP we will still get a\n   702→     response */\n   703→  if(data->state.upload &&\n   704→     !(conn->handler->protocol&(PROTO_FAMILY_HTTP|CURLPROTO_RTSP)))\n   705→    return CURLE_OK;\n   706→\n   707→  if((data->req.bytecount + data->req.headerbytecount == 0) &&\n   708→     conn->bits.reuse &&\n   709→     (!data->req.no_body || (conn->handler->protocol & PROTO_FAMILY_HTTP))\n   710→#ifndef CURL_DISABLE_RTSP\n   711→     && (data->set.rtspreq != RTSPREQ_RECEIVE)\n   712→#endif\n   713→    )\n   714→    /* We got no data, we attempted to reuse a connection. For HTTP this\n   715→       can be a retry so we try again regardless if we expected a body.\n   716→       For other protocols we only try again only if we expected a body.\n   717→\n   718→       This might happen if the connection was left alive when we were\n   719→       done using it before, but that was closed when we wanted to read from\n   720→       it again. Bad luck. Retry the same request on a fresh connect! */\n   721→    retry = TRUE;\n   722→  else if(data->state.refused_stream &&\n   723→          (data->req.bytecount + data->req.headerbytecount == 0) ) {\n   724→    /* This was sent on a refused stream, safe to rerun. A refused stream\n   725→       error can typically only happen on HTTP/2 level if the stream is safe\n   726→       to issue again, but the nghttp2 API can deliver the message to other\n   727→       streams as well, which is why this adds the check the data counters\n   728→       too. */\n   729→    infof(data, \"REFUSED_STREAM, retrying a fresh connect\");\n   730→    data->state.refused_stream = FALSE; /* clear again */\n   731→    retry = TRUE;\n   732→  }\n   733→  if(retry) {\n   734→#define CONN_MAX_RETRIES 5\n   735→    if(data->state.retrycount++ >= CONN_MAX_RETRIES) {\n   736→      failf(data, \"Connection died, tried %d times before giving up\",\n   737→            CONN_MAX_RETRIES);\n   738→      data->state.retrycount = 0;\n   739→      return CURLE_SEND_ERROR;\n   740→    }\n   741→    infof(data, \"Connection died, retrying a fresh connect (retry count: %d)\",\n   742→          data->state.retrycount);\n   743→    *url = strdup(data->state.url);\n   744→    if(!*url)\n   745→      return CURLE_OUT_OF_MEMORY;\n   746→\n   747→    connclose(conn, \"retry\"); /* close this connection */\n   748→    conn->bits.retry = TRUE; /* mark this as a connection we are about\n   749→                                to retry. Marking it this way should\n   750→                                prevent i.e HTTP transfers to return\n   751→                                error just because nothing has been\n   752→                                transferred! */\n   753→    Curl_creader_set_rewind(data, TRUE);\n   754→  }\n   755→  return CURLE_OK;\n   756→}\n   757→\n   758→/*\n   759→ * xfer_setup() is called to setup basic properties for the transfer.\n   760→ */\n   761→static void xfer_setup(\n   762→  struct Curl_easy *data,   /* transfer */\n   763→  int sockindex,            /* socket index to read from or -1 */\n   764→  curl_off_t size,          /* -1 if unknown at this point */\n   765→  bool getheader,           /* TRUE if header parsing is wanted */\n   766→  int writesockindex,       /* socket index to write to, it may be the same we\n   767→                               read from. -1 disables */\n   768→  bool shutdown,            /* shutdown connection at transfer end. Only\n   769→                             * supported when sending OR receiving. */\n   770→  bool shutdown_err_ignore  /* errors during shutdown do not fail the\n   771→                             * transfer */\n   772→  )\n   773→{\n   774→  struct SingleRequest *k = &data->req;\n   775→  struct connectdata *conn = data->conn;\n   776→  bool want_send = Curl_req_want_send(data);\n   777→\n   778→  DEBUGASSERT(conn != NULL);\n   779→  DEBUGASSERT((sockindex <= 1) && (sockindex >= -1));\n   780→  DEBUGASSERT((writesockindex <= 1) && (writesockindex >= -1));\n   781→  DEBUGASSERT(!shutdown || (sockindex == -1) || (writesockindex == -1));\n   782→\n   783→  if(Curl_conn_is_multiplex(conn, FIRSTSOCKET) || want_send) {\n   784→    /* when multiplexing, the read/write sockets need to be the same! */\n   785→    conn->sockfd = sockindex == -1 ?\n   786→      ((writesockindex == -1 ? CURL_SOCKET_BAD : conn->sock[writesockindex])) :\n   787→      conn->sock[sockindex];\n   788→    conn->writesockfd = conn->sockfd;\n   789→    if(want_send)\n   790→      /* special and HTTP-specific */\n   791→      writesockindex = FIRSTSOCKET;\n   792→  }\n   793→  else {\n   794→    conn->sockfd = sockindex == -1 ?\n   795→      CURL_SOCKET_BAD : conn->sock[sockindex];\n   796→    conn->writesockfd = writesockindex == -1 ?\n   797→      CURL_SOCKET_BAD : conn->sock[writesockindex];\n   798→  }\n   799→\n   800→  k->getheader = getheader;\n   801→  k->size = size;\n   802→  k->shutdown = shutdown;\n   803→  k->shutdown_err_ignore = shutdown_err_ignore;\n   804→\n   805→  /* The code sequence below is placed in this function just because all\n   806→     necessary input is not always known in do_complete() as this function may\n   807→     be called after that */\n   808→\n   809→  if(!k->getheader) {\n   810→    k->header = FALSE;\n   811→    if(size > 0)\n   812→      Curl_pgrsSetDownloadSize(data, size);\n   813→  }\n   814→  /* we want header and/or body, if neither then do not do this! */\n   815→  if(k->getheader || !data->req.no_body) {\n   816→\n   817→    if(sockindex != -1)\n   818→      k->keepon |= KEEP_RECV;\n   819→\n   820→    if(writesockindex != -1)\n   821→      k->keepon |= KEEP_SEND;\n   822→  } /* if(k->getheader || !data->req.no_body) */\n   823→\n   824→}\n   825→\n   826→void Curl_xfer_setup_nop(struct Curl_easy *data)\n   827→{\n   828→  xfer_setup(data, -1, -1, FALSE, -1, FALSE, FALSE);\n   829→}\n   830→\n   831→void Curl_xfer_setup1(struct Curl_easy *data,\n   832→                      int send_recv,\n   833→                      curl_off_t recv_size,\n   834→                      bool getheader)\n   835→{\n   836→  int recv_index = (send_recv & CURL_XFER_RECV) ? FIRSTSOCKET : -1;\n   837→  int send_index = (send_recv & CURL_XFER_SEND) ? FIRSTSOCKET : -1;\n   838→  DEBUGASSERT((recv_index >= 0) || (recv_size == -1));\n   839→  xfer_setup(data, recv_index, recv_size, getheader, send_index, FALSE, FALSE);\n   840→}\n   841→\n   842→void Curl_xfer_setup2(struct Curl_easy *data,\n   843→                      int send_recv,\n   844→                      curl_off_t recv_size,\n   845→                      bool shutdown,\n   846→                      bool shutdown_err_ignore)\n   847→{\n   848→  int recv_index = (send_recv & CURL_XFER_RECV) ? SECONDARYSOCKET : -1;\n   849→  int send_index = (send_recv & CURL_XFER_SEND) ? SECONDARYSOCKET : -1;\n   850→  DEBUGASSERT((recv_index >= 0) || (recv_size == -1));\n   851→  xfer_setup(data, recv_index, recv_size, FALSE, send_index,\n   852→             shutdown, shutdown_err_ignore);\n   853→}\n   854→\n   855→CURLcode Curl_xfer_write_resp(struct Curl_easy *data,\n   856→                              const char *buf, size_t blen,\n   857→                              bool is_eos)\n   858→{\n   859→  CURLcode result = CURLE_OK;\n   860→\n   861→  if(data->conn->handler->write_resp) {\n   862→    /* protocol handlers offering this function take full responsibility\n   863→     * for writing all received download data to the client. */\n   864→    result = data->conn->handler->write_resp(data, buf, blen, is_eos);\n   865→  }\n   866→  else {\n   867→    /* No special handling by protocol handler, write all received data\n   868→     * as BODY to the client. */\n   869→    if(blen || is_eos) {\n   870→      int cwtype = CLIENTWRITE_BODY;\n   871→      if(is_eos)\n   872→        cwtype |= CLIENTWRITE_EOS;\n   873→      result = Curl_client_write(data, cwtype, buf, blen);\n   874→    }\n   875→  }\n   876→\n   877→  if(!result && is_eos) {\n   878→    /* If we wrote the EOS, we are definitely done */\n   879→    data->req.eos_written = TRUE;\n   880→    data->req.download_done = TRUE;\n   881→  }\n   882→  CURL_TRC_WRITE(data, !defined(CURL_DISABLE_IMAP)\n/*\n * checkheaders() checks the linked list of custom headers for a\n * particular header (prefix). bytes read or -1 for error\n */\nstatic ssize_t xfer_recv_resp(struct Curl_easy *data,\n                              char *buf, size_t blen,\n                              bool eos_reliable,\n                              CURLcode *err)\n{\n  ssize_t nread;\n\n  DEBUGASSERT(blen > 0);\n  /* If we are reading BODY data and the connection does NOT handle EOF\n   * and we know the size of the BODY data, limit the read amount */\n  if(!eos_reliable && !data->req.header && data->req.size != -1) {\n    curl_off_t totalleft = data->req.size - data->req.bytecount;\n    if(totalleft <= 0)\n      blen = 0;\n    else if(totalleft < (curl_off_t)blen)\n      blen = (size_t)totalleft;\n  }\n  else if(xfer_recv_shutdown_started(data)) {\n    /* we already received everything. Do not try more. */\n    blen = 0;\n  }\n\n  if(!blen) {\n    /* want nothing more */\n    *err = CURLE_OK;\n    nread = 0;\n  }\n  else {\n    *err = Curl_xfer_recv(data, buf, blen, &nread);\n  }\n\n  if(*err)\n    return -1;\n  if(nread == 0) {\n    if(data->req.shutdown) {\n      bool done;\n      *err = xfer_recv_shutdown(data, &done);\n      if(*err)\n        return -1;\n      if(!done) {\n        *err = CURLE_AGAIN;\n        return -1;\n      }\n    }\n    DEBUGF(infof(data, \"sendrecv_dl: we are done\"));\n  }\n  DEBUGASSERT(nread >= 0);\n  return nread;\n}\n\n/*\n * Go ahead and do a read if we have a readable socket or if\n * the stream was rewound (in which case we have data in a\n * buffer)\n */\nstatic CURLcode sendrecv_dl(struct Curl_easy *data,\n                            struct SingleRequest *k,\n                            int *didwhat)\n{\n  struct connectdata *conn = data->conn;\n  CURLcode result = CURLE_OK;\n  char *buf, *xfer_buf;\n  size_t blen, xfer_blen;\n  int maxloops = 10;\n  curl_off_t total_received = 0;\n  bool is_multiplex = FALSE;\n\n  result = Curl_multi_xfer_buf_borrow(data, &xfer_buf, &xfer_blen);\n  if(result)\n    goto out;\n\n  /* This is where we loop until we have read everything there is to\n     read or we get a CURLE_AGAIN */\n  do {\n    bool is_eos = FALSE;\n    size_t bytestoread;\n    ssize_t nread;\n\n    if(!is_multiplex) {\n      /* Multiplexed connection have inherent handling of EOF and we do not\n       * have to carefully restrict the amount we try to read.\n       * Multiplexed changes only in one direction. */\n      is_multiplex = Curl_conn_is_multiplex(conn, FIRSTSOCKET);\n    }\n\n    buf = xfer_buf;\n    bytestoread = xfer_blen;\n\n    if(bytestoread && data->set.max_recv_speed > 0) {\n      /* In case of speed limit on receiving: if this loop already got\n       * data, break out. On multiplexed connections,\n     * we should read the EOS. Which may arrive as meta data after\n     * the bytes. Not taking it in might lead to RST of streams. */\n    if((!is_multiplex && data->req.download_done) || is_eos) {\n      data->req.keepon &= ~KEEP_RECV;\n    }\n    /* if we are PAUSEd or stopped receiving, leave the loop */\n    if((k->keepon & KEEP_RECV_PAUSE) || !(k->keepon & KEEP_RECV))\n      break;\n\n  } while(maxloops--);\n\n  if((maxloops <= 0) || data_pending(data)) {\n    /* did not read until EAGAIN or there is still pending data, mark as\n       read-again-please */\n    data->state.select_bits = CURL_CSELECT_IN;\n    if((k->keepon & KEEP_SENDBITS) == KEEP_SEND)\n      data->state.select_bits |= CURL_CSELECT_OUT;\n  }\n\n  if(((k->keepon & (KEEP_RECV|KEEP_SEND)) == KEEP_SEND) &&\n     (conn->bits.close || is_multiplex)) {\n    /* When we have read the entire thing and the close bit is set, the server\n       may now close the connection. If there is now any kind of sending going\n       on from our side, we need to stop that immediately. */\n    infof(data, \"we are done reading and this is set to close, stop send\");\n    Curl_req_abort_sending(data);\n  }\n\nout:\n  Curl_multi_xfer_buf_release(data, xfer_buf);\n  if(result)\n    DEBUGF(infof(data, \"sendrecv_dl() -> %d\", result));\n  return result;\n}\n\n/*\n * Send data to upload to the server, when the socket is writable.\n */\nstatic CURLcode sendrecv_ul(struct Curl_easy *data, int *didwhat)\n{\n  /* We should not get here when the sending is already done. It\n   * probably means that someone set `data-req.keepon |= KEEP_SEND`\n   * when it should not. */\n  DEBUGASSERT(!Curl_req_done_sending(data));\n\n  if(!Curl_req_done_sending(data)) {\n    *didwhat |= KEEP_SEND;\n    return Curl_req_send_more(data);\n  }\n  return CURLE_OK;\n}\n\nstatic int select_bits_paused(struct Curl_easy *data, int select_bits)\n{\n  /* See issue #11982: we really need to be careful not to progress\n   * a transfer direction when that direction is paused. Not all parts\n   * of our state machine are handling PAUSED transfers correctly. So, we\n   * do not want to go there.\n   * NOTE: we are only interested in PAUSE, not HOLD. */\n\n  /* if there is data in a direction not paused, return false */\n  if(((select_bits & (data->req.keepon & (KEEP_RECV_PAUSE|KEEP_SEND_PAUSE));\n}\n\n/*\n * Curl_sendrecv() is the low-level function to be called when data is to\n * be read and written to/from the connection.\n */\nCURLcode Curl_sendrecv(struct Curl_easy *data, struct curltime *nowp)\n{\n  struct SingleRequest *k = &data->req;\n  CURLcode result = CURLE_OK;\n  int didwhat = 0;\n\n  DEBUGASSERT(nowp);\n */\n      result = CURLE_OK;\n      goto out;\n    }\n    data->state.select_bits = 0;\n  }\n\n  /* We go ahead and do a read if we have a readable socket or if the stream\n     was rewound (in which data->req.done = TRUE;\n\nout:\n  if(result)\n    DEBUGF(infof(data, \"Curl_sendrecv() -> %d\", result));\n  return result;\n}\n\n/* Curl_init_CONNECT() gets called each time the handle switches to (from RFC6265bis draft-19)\n\n   For the sake of easier testing, align the capped time to an even 60 second\n   boundary.\n*/\nstatic void cap_expires(time_t now, struct Cookie *co)\n{\n  if((TIME_T_MAX - COOKIES_MAXAGE - 30) > now) {\n    timediff_t cap = now + COOKIES_MAXAGE;\n    if(co->expires > cap) {\n      cap += 30;\n      co->expires = (cap/60)*60;\n    }\n  }\n}\n\nstatic void freecookie(struct Cookie *co)\n{\n  free(co->domain);\n  free(co->path);\n  free(co->spath);\n  free(co->name);\n  free(co->value);\n  free(co);\n}\n\nstatic bool cookie_tailmatch(const char *cookie_domain,\n                             size_t cookie_domain_len,\n                             const char *hostname)\n{\n  size_t hostname_len = strlen(hostname);\n\n  if(hostname_len < cookie_domain_len)\n    return FALSE;\n\n  if(!strncasecompare(cookie_domain,\n                      hostname + hostname_len-cookie_domain_len,\n                      cookie_domain_len))\n    return FALSE;\n\n  /*\n   * A lead char of cookie_domain is not '.'.\n   * RFC6265 4.1.2.3. The Domain Attribute says:\n   * For example, if the value of the Domain attribute is\n   * \"example.com\", the user agent will include the cookie in the Cookie\n   * header when making HTTP requests to example.com, www.example.com, and\n   * www.corp.example.com.\n   */\n  if(hostname_len == cookie_domain_len)\n    return TRUE;\n  if('.' == *(hostname + hostname_len - cookie_domain_len))\n    return TRUE;\n  return FALSE;\n}\n\n/*\n * matching cookie path and URL path\n * RFC6265 5.1.4 Paths and Path-Match\n */\nstatic bool pathmatch(const char *cookie_path, const char *request_uri)\n{\n  size_t cookie_path_len;\n  size_t uri_path_len;\n  char *uri_path = NULL;\n  char *pos;\n  bool ret = FALSE;\n\n  /* cookie_path must not have last '/' separator. ex: /sample */\n  cookie_path_len = strlen(cookie_path);\n  if(1 == cookie_path_len) {\n    /* cookie_path must be '/' */\n    return TRUE;\n  }\n\n  uri_path = strdup(request_uri);\n  if(!uri_path)\n    return FALSE;\n  pos = strchr(uri_path, '?');\n  if(pos)\n    *pos = 0x0;\n\n  /* #-fragments are already cut off! */\n  if(0 == strlen(uri_path) || uri_path[0] != '/') {\n    strstore(&uri_path, \"/\", 1);\n    if(!uri_path)\n      return FALSE;\n  }\n\n  /*\n   * here, RFC6265 5.1.4 says\n   *  4. Output the characters of the uri-path from the first character up\n   *     to, but not including, the right-most %x2F (\"/\").\n   *  but URL path /hoge?fuga=xxx means /hoge/index.cgi?fuga=xxx in some site\n   *  without redirect.\n   *  Ignore this algorithm because /hoge is uri path for this case\n   *  (uri path is not /).\n   */\n\n  uri_path_len = strlen(uri_path);\n\n  if(uri_path_len < cookie_path_len) {\n    ret = FALSE;\n    goto pathmatched;\n  }\n\n  /* not using checkprefix() because matching should be case-sensitive */\n  if(strncmp(cookie_path, uri_path, cookie_path_len)) {\n    ret = FALSE;\n    goto pathmatched;\n  }\n\n  /* The cookie-path and the uri-path are identical. */\n  if(cookie_path_len == uri_path_len) {\n    ret = TRUE;\n    goto pathmatched;\n  }\n\n  /* here, cookie_path_len < uri_path_len */\n  if(uri_path[cookie_path_len] == '/') {\n    ret = TRUE;\n    goto pathmatched;\n  }\n\n  ret = FALSE;\n\npathmatched:\n  free(uri_path);\n  return ret;\n}\n\n/*\n * Return the top-level domain, for optimal hashing.\n */\nstatic const char *get_top_domain(const char * const domain, size_t *outlen)\n{\n  size_t len = 0;\n  const char *first = NULL, *last;\n\n  if(domain) {\n    len = strlen(domain);\n    last = memrchr(domain, '.', len);\n    if(last) {\n      first = memrchr(domain, '.', (last - domain));\n      if(first)\n        len -= (++first - domain);\n    }\n  }\n\n  if(outlen)\n    *outlen = len;\n\n  return first ? first : domain;\n}\n\n/* Avoid C1001, an \"internal error\" with MSVC14 */\n#if defined(_MSC_VER) && (_MSC_VER == 1900)\n#pragma optimize(\"\", off)\n#endif\n\n/*\n * A case-insensitive hash for the cookie domains.\n */\nstatic size_t cookie_hash_domain(const char *domain, const size_t len)\n{\n  const char *end = domain + len;\n  size_t h = 5381;\n\n  while(domain < end) {\n    size_t j = (size_t)Curl_raw_toupper(*domain++);\n    h += h << 5;\n    h ^= j;\n  }\n\n  return (h % COOKIE_HASH_SIZE);\n}\n\n#if defined(_MSC_VER) && (_MSC_VER == 1900)\n#pragma optimize(\"\", on)\n#endif\n\n/*\n * Hash this domain.\n */\nstatic size_t cookiehash(const char * const domain)\n{\n  const char *top;\n  size_t len;\n\n  if(!domain || Curl_host_is_ipnum(domain))\n    return 0;\n\n  top = get_top_domain(domain, &len);\n  return cookie_hash_domain(top, len);\n}\n\n/*\n * cookie path sanitize\n */\nstatic char *sanitize_cookie_path(const char *cookie_path)\n{\n  size_t len;\n  char *new_path = strdup(cookie_path);\n  if(!new_path)\n    return NULL;\n\n  /* some stupid site sends path attribute with '\"'. */\n  len = strlen(new_path);\n  if(new_path[0] == '\\\"') {\n    memmove(new_path, new_path + 1, len);\n    len--;\n  }\n  if(len && (new_path[len - 1] == '\\\"')) {\n    new_path[--len] = 0x0;\n  }\n\n  /* RFC6265 5.2.4 The Path Attribute */\n  if(new_path[0] != '/') {\n    /* Let cookie-path be the default-path. */\n    strstore(&new_path, \"/\", 1);\n    return new_path;\n  }\n\n  /* convert /hoge/ to /hoge */\n  if(len && new_path[len - 1] == '/') {\n    new_path[len - 1] = 0x0;\n  }\n\n  return new_path;\n}\n\n/*\n * Load cookies from all given cookie files (CURLOPT_COOKIEFILE).\n *\n * NOTE: OOM or cookie parsing failures are ignored.\n */\nvoid Curl_cookie_loadfiles(struct Curl_easy *data)\n{\n  struct curl_slist *list = data->state.cookielist;\n  if(list) {\n    Curl_share_lock(data, CURL_LOCK_DATA_COOKIE, CURL_LOCK_ACCESS_SINGLE);\n    while(list) {\n      struct CookieInfo *ci =\n        Curl_cookie_init(data, list->data, data->cookies,\n                         data->set.cookiesession);\n      if(!ci)\n        /*\n         * Failure may be due to OOM or a bad cookie; both are ignored\n         * but only the first should be\n         */\n        infof(data, \"ignoring failed cookie_init for %s\", list->data);\n      else\n        data->cookies = ci;\n      list = list->next;\n    }\n    Curl_share_unlock(data, CURL_LOCK_DATA_COOKIE);\n  }\n}\n\n/*\n * strstore\n *\n * A thin wrapper around strdup which ensures that any memory allocated at\n * *str will be freed before the string allocated by strdup is stored there.\n * The intended usecase is repeated assignments to the same variable during\n * parsing in a last-wins scenario. The caller is responsible for checking\n * for OOM errors.\n */\nstatic void strstore(char **str, const char *newstr, size_t len)\n{\n  DEBUGASSERT(newstr);\n  DEBUGASSERT(str);\n  free(*str);\n  *str = Curl_memdup0(newstr, len);\n}\n\n/*\n * remove_expired\n *\n * Remove expired cookies from the hash by inspecting the expires timestamp on\n * each cookie in the hash, freeing and deleting any where the timestamp is in\n * the past. If the cookiejar has recorded the next timestamp at which one or\n * more cookies expire, then processing will exit early in case this timestamp\n * is in the future.\n */\nstatic void remove_expired(struct CookieInfo *ci)\n{\n  struct Cookie *co;\n  curl_off_t now = (curl_off_t)time(NULL);\n  unsigned int i;\n\n  /*\n   * If the earliest expiration timestamp in the jar is in the future we can\n   * skip scanning the whole jar and instead exit early as there will not be\n   * any cookies to evict. If we need to evict however, reset the\n   * next_expiration counter in order to track the next one. In case the\n   * recorded first expiration is the max offset, then perform the safe\n   * fallback of checking all cookies.\n   */\n  if(now < ci->next_expiration &&\n     ci->next_expiration != CURL_OFF_T_MAX)\n    return;\n  else\n    ci->next_expiration = CURL_OFF_T_MAX;\n\n  for(i = 0; i < COOKIE_HASH_SIZE; i++) {\n    struct Curl_llist_node *n;\n    struct Curl_llist_node *e = NULL;\n\n    for(n = Curl_llist_head(&ci->cookielist[i]); n; n = e) {\n      co = Curl_node_elem(n);\n      e = Curl_node_next(n);\n      if(co->expires && co->expires < now) {\n        Curl_node_remove(n);\n        freecookie(co);\n        ci->numcookies--;\n      }\n      else {\n        /*\n         * If this cookie has an expiration timestamp earlier than what we\n         * have seen so far then record it for the next round of expirations.\n         */\n        if(co->expires && co->expires < ci->next_expiration)\n          ci->next_expiration = co->expires;\n      }\n    }\n  }\n}\n\n#ifndef USE_LIBPSL\n/* Make sure domain contains a dot or is localhost. */\nstatic bool bad_domain(const char *domain, size_t len)\n{\n  if((len == 9) && strncasecompare(domain, \"localhost\", 9))\n    return FALSE;\n  else {\n    /* there must be a dot present, but that dot must not be a trailing dot */\n    char *dot = memchr(domain, '.', len);\n    if(dot) {\n      size_t i = dot - domain;\n      if((len - i) > 1)\n        /* the dot is not the last byte */\n        return FALSE;\n    }\n  }\n  return TRUE;\n}\n#endif\n\n/*\n  RFC 6265 section 4.1.1 says a server should accept this range:\n\n  cookie-octet    = %x21 / %x23-2B / %x2D-3A / %x3C-5B / %x5D-7E\n\n  But Firefox and Chrome as of June 2022 accept space, comma and double-quotes\n  fine. The prime reason for filtering out control bytes is that some HTTP\n  servers return 400 for requests that contain such.\n*/\nstatic bool invalid_octets(const char *p)\n{\n  /* Reject all bytes \\x01 - \\x1f (*except* \\x09, TAB) + \\x7f */\n  static const char badoctets[] = {\n    \"\\x01\\x02\\x03\\x04\\x05\\x06\\x07\\x08\\x0a\"\n    \"\\x0b\\x0c\\x0d\\x0e\\x0f\\x10\\x11\\x12\\x13\\x14\"\n    \"\\x15\\x16\\x17\\x18\\x19\\x1a\\x1b\\x1c\\x1d\\x1e\\x1f\\x7f\"\n  };\n  size_t len;\n  /* scan for all the octets that are *not* in cookie-octet */\n  len = strcspn(p, badoctets);\n  return p[len] != '\\0';\n}\n\n#define CERR_OK            0\n#define CERR_TOO_LONG      1 /* input line too long */\n#define CERR_TAB           2 /* in a wrong place */\n#define CERR_TOO_BIG       3 /* name/value too large */\n#define CERR_BAD           4 /* deemed incorrect */\n#define CERR_NO_SEP        5 /* semicolon problem */\n#define CERR_NO_NAME_VALUE 6 /* name or value problem */\n#define CERR_INVALID_OCTET 7 /* bad content */\n#define CERR_BAD_SECURE    8 /* secure in a bad place */\n#define CERR_OUT_OF_MEMORY 9\n#define CERR_NO_TAILMATCH  10\n#define CERR_COMMENT       11 /* a commented line */\n#define CERR_RANGE         12 /* expire range problem */\n#define CERR_FIELDS        13 /* incomplete netscape line */\n#define CERR_PSL           14 /* a public suffix */\n#define CERR_LIVE_WINS     15\n\n/* The maximum length we accept a date string for the 'expire' keyword. The\n   standard date formats are within the 30 bytes range. This adds an extra\n   margin just to make sure it realistically works with what is used out\n   there.\n*/\n#define MAX_DATE_LENGTH 80\n\nstatic int\nparse_cookie_header(struct Curl_easy *data,\n                    struct Cookie *co,\n                    struct CookieInfo *ci,\n                    const char *ptr,\n                    const char *domain, /* default domain */\n                    const char *path,   /* full path used when this cookie is\n                                           set, used to get default path for\n                                           the cookie unless set */\n                    bool secure)  /* TRUE if connection is over secure\n                                     origin */\n{\n  /* This line was read off an HTTP-header */\n  time_t now;\n  size_t linelength = strlen(ptr);\n  if(linelength > MAX_COOKIE_LINE)\n    /* discard overly long lines at once */\n    return CERR_TOO_LONG;\n\n  now = time(NULL);\n  do {\n    size_t vlen;\n    size_t nlen;\n\n    while(*ptr && ISBLANK(*ptr))\n      ptr++;\n\n    /* we have a <name>=<value> pair or a stand-alone word here */\n    nlen = strcspn(ptr, \";\\t\\r\\n=\");\n    if(nlen) {\n      bool done = FALSE;\n      bool sep = FALSE;\n      const char *namep = ptr;\n      const char *valuep;\n\n      ptr += nlen;\n\n      /* trim trailing spaces and tabs after name */\n      while(nlen && ISBLANK(namep[nlen - 1]))\n        nlen--;\n\n      if(*ptr == '=') {\n        vlen = strcspn(++ptr, \";\\r\\n\");\n        valuep = ptr;\n        sep = TRUE;\n        ptr = &valuep[vlen];\n\n        /* Strip off trailing whitespace from the value */\n        while(vlen && ISBLANK(valuep[vlen-1]))\n          vlen--;\n\n        /* Skip leading whitespace from the value */\n        while(vlen && ISBLANK(*valuep)) {\n          valuep++;\n          vlen--;\n        }\n\n        /* Reject cookies with a TAB inside the value */\n        if(memchr(valuep, '\\t', vlen)) {\n          infof(data, \"cookie contains TAB, dropping\");\n          return CERR_TAB;\n        }\n      }\n      else {\n        valuep = NULL;\n        vlen = 0;\n      }\n\n      /*\n       * Check for too long individual name or contents, or too long\n       * combination of name + contents. Chrome and Firefox support 4095 or\n       * 4096 bytes combo\n       */\n      if(nlen >= (MAX_NAME-1) || vlen >= (MAX_NAME-1) ||\n         ((nlen + vlen) > MAX_NAME)) {\n        infof(data, \"oversized cookie dropped, name/val %zu + %zu bytes\",\n              nlen, vlen);\n        return CERR_TOO_BIG;\n      }\n\n      /*\n       * Check if we have a reserved prefix set before anything else, as we\n       * otherwise have to test for the prefix in both the cookie name and\n       * \"the rest\". Prefixes must start with '__' and end with a '-', so\n       * only test for names where that can possibly be true.\n       */\n      if(nlen >= 7 && namep[0] == '_' && namep[1] == '_') {\n        if(strncasecompare(\"__Secure-\", namep, 9))\n          co->prefix_secure = TRUE;\n        else if(strncasecompare(\"__Host-\", namep, 7))\n          co->prefix_host = TRUE;\n      }\n\n      /*\n       * Use strstore() below to properly deal with received cookie\n       * headers that have the same string property set more than once,\n       * and then we use the last one.\n       */\n\n      if(!co->name) {\n        /* The very first name/value pair is the actual cookie name */\n        if(!sep)\n          /* Bad name/value pair. */\n          return CERR_NO_SEP;\n\n        strstore(&co->name, namep, nlen);\n        strstore(&co->value, valuep, vlen);\n        done = TRUE;\n        if(!co->name || !co->value)\n          return CERR_NO_NAME_VALUE;\n\n        if(invalid_octets(co->value) || invalid_octets(co->name)) {\n          infof(data, \"invalid octets in name/value, cookie dropped\");\n          return CERR_INVALID_OCTET;\n        }\n      }\n      else if(!vlen) {\n        /*\n         * this was a \"<name>=\" with no content, and we must allow\n         * 'secure' and 'httponly' specified this weirdly\n         */\n        done = TRUE;\n        /*\n         * secure cookies are only allowed to be set when the connection is\n         * using a secure protocol, or when the cookie is being set by\n         * reading from file\n         */\n        if((nlen == 6) && strncasecompare(\"secure\", namep, 6)) {\n          if(secure || !ci->running) {\n            co->secure = TRUE;\n          }\n          else {\n            return CERR_BAD_SECURE;\n          }\n        }\n        else if((nlen == 8) && strncasecompare(\"httponly\", namep, 8))\n          co->httponly = TRUE;\n        else if(sep)\n          /* there was a '=' so we are not done parsing this field */\n          done = FALSE;\n      }\n      if(done)\n        ;\n      else if((nlen == 4) && strncasecompare(\"path\", namep, 4)) {\n        strstore(&co->path, valuep, vlen);\n        if(!co->path)\n          return CERR_OUT_OF_MEMORY;\n        free(co->spath); /* if this is set again */\n        co->spath = sanitize_cookie_path(co->path);\n        if(!co->spath)\n          return CERR_OUT_OF_MEMORY;\n      }\n      else if((nlen == 6) &&\n              strncasecompare(\"domain\", namep, 6) && vlen) {\n        bool is_ip;\n\n        /*\n         * Now, we make sure that our host is within the given domain, or\n         * the given domain is not valid and thus cannot be set.\n         */\n\n        if('.' == valuep[0]) {\n          valuep++; /* ignore preceding dot */\n          vlen--;\n        }\n\n#ifndef USE_LIBPSL\n        /*\n         * Without PSL we do not know when the incoming cookie is set on a\n         * TLD or otherwise \"protected\" suffix. To reduce risk, we require a\n         * dot OR the exact hostname being \"localhost\".\n         */\n        if(bad_domain(valuep, vlen))\n          domain = \":\";\n#endif\n\n        is_ip = Curl_host_is_ipnum(domain ? domain : valuep);\n\n        if(!domain\n           || (is_ip && !strncmp(valuep, domain, vlen) &&\n               (vlen == strlen(domain)))\n           || (!is_ip && cookie_tailmatch(valuep, vlen, domain))) {\n          strstore(&co->domain, valuep, vlen);\n          if(!co->domain)\n            return CERR_OUT_OF_MEMORY;\n\n          if(!is_ip)\n            co->tailmatch = TRUE; /* we always do that if the domain name was\n                                     given */\n        }\n        else {\n          /*\n           * We did not get a tailmatch and then the attempted set domain is\n           * not a domain to which the current host belongs. Mark as bad.\n           */\n          infof(data, \"skipped cookie with bad tailmatch domain: %s\",\n                valuep);\n          return CERR_NO_TAILMATCH;\n        }\n      }\n      else if((nlen == 7) && strncasecompare(\"version\", namep, 7)) {\n        /* just ignore */\n      }\n      else if((nlen == 7) && strncasecompare(\"max-age\", namep, 7)) {\n        /*\n         * Defined in RFC2109:\n         *\n         * Optional. The Max-Age attribute defines the lifetime of the\n         * cookie, in seconds. The delta-seconds value is a decimal non-\n         * negative integer. After delta-seconds seconds elapse, the\n         * client should discard the cookie. A value of zero means the\n         * cookie should be discarded immediately.\n         */\n        CURLofft offt;\n        const char *maxage = valuep;\n        offt = curlx_strtoofft((*maxage == '\\\"') ?\n                               &maxage[1] : &maxage[0], NULL, 10,\n                               &co->expires);\n        switch(offt) {\n        case CURL_OFFT_FLOW:\n          /* overflow, used max value */\n          co->expires = CURL_OFF_T_MAX;\n          break;\n        case CURL_OFFT_INVAL:\n          /* negative or otherwise bad, expire */\n          co->expires = 1;\n          break;\n        case CURL_OFFT_OK:\n          if(!co->expires)\n            /* already expired */\n            co->expires = 1;\n          else if(CURL_OFF_T_MAX - now < co->expires)\n            /* would overflow */\n            co->expires = CURL_OFF_T_MAX;\n          else\n            co->expires += now;\n          break;\n        }\n        cap_expires(now, co);\n      }\n      else if((nlen == 7) && strncasecompare(\"expires\", namep, 7)) {\n        if(!co->expires && (vlen < MAX_DATE_LENGTH)) {\n          /*\n           * Let max-age have priority.\n           *\n           * If the date cannot get parsed for whatever reason, the cookie\n           * will be treated as a session cookie\n           */\n          char dbuf[MAX_DATE_LENGTH + 1];\n          memcpy(dbuf, valuep, vlen);\n          dbuf[vlen] = 0;\n          co->expires = Curl_getdate_capped(dbuf);\n\n          /*\n           * Session cookies have expires set to 0 so if we get that back\n           * from the date parser let's add a second to make it a\n           * non-session cookie\n           */\n          if(co->expires == 0)\n            co->expires = 1;\n          else if(co->expires < 0)\n            co->expires = 0;\n          cap_expires(now, co);\n        }\n      }\n\n      /*\n       * Else, this is the second (or more) name we do not know about!\n       */\n    }\n    else {\n      /* this is an \"illegal\" <what>=<this> pair */\n    }\n\n    while(*ptr && ISBLANK(*ptr))\n      ptr++;\n    if(*ptr == ';')\n      ptr++;\n    else\n      break;\n  } while(1);\n\n  if(!co->domain && domain) {\n    /* no domain was given in the header line, set the default */\n    co->domain = strdup(domain);\n    if(!co->domain)\n      return CERR_OUT_OF_MEMORY;\n  }\n\n  if(!co->path && path) {\n    /*\n     * No path was given in the header line, set the default. Note that the\n     * passed-in path to this function MAY have a '?' and following part that\n     * MUST NOT be stored as part of the path.\n     */\n    char *queryp = strchr(path, '?');\n\n    /*\n     * queryp is where the interesting part of the path ends, so now we\n     * want to the find the last\n     */\n    char *endslash;\n    if(!queryp)\n      endslash = strrchr(path, '/');\n    else\n      endslash = memrchr(path, '/', (queryp - path));\n    if(endslash) {\n      size_t pathlen = (endslash-path + 1); /* include end slash */\n      co->path = Curl_memdup0(path, pathlen);\n      if(co->path) {\n        co->spath = sanitize_cookie_path(co->path);\n        if(!co->spath)\n          return CERR_OUT_OF_MEMORY;\n      }\n      else\n        return CERR_OUT_OF_MEMORY;\n    }\n  }\n\n  /*\n   * If we did not get a cookie name, or a bad one, the this is an illegal\n   * line so bail out.\n   */\n  if(!co->name)\n    return CERR_BAD;\n\n  data->req.setcookies++;\n  return CERR_OK;\n}\n\nstatic int\nparse_netscape(struct Cookie *co,\n               struct CookieInfo *ci,\n               const char *lineptr,\n               bool secure)  /* TRUE if connection is over secure\n                                origin */\n{\n  /*\n   * This line is NOT an HTTP header style line, we do offer support for\n   * reading the odd netscape cookies-file format here\n   */\n  const char *ptr, *next;\n  int fields;\n  size_t len;\n\n  /*\n   * In 2008, Internet Explorer introduced HTTP-only cookies to prevent XSS\n   * attacks. Cookies marked httpOnly are not accessible to JavaScript. In\n   * Firefox's cookie files, they are prefixed #HttpOnly_ and the rest\n   * remains as usual, so we skip 10 characters of the line.\n   */\n  if(strncmp(lineptr, \"#HttpOnly_\", 10) == 0) {\n    lineptr += 10;\n    co->httponly = TRUE;\n  }\n\n  if(lineptr[0]=='#')\n    /* do not even try the comments */\n    return CERR_COMMENT;\n\n  /*\n   * Now loop through the fields and init the struct we already have\n   * allocated\n   */\n  fields = 0;\n  for(next = lineptr; next; fields++) {\n    ptr = next;\n    len = strcspn(ptr, \"\\t\\r\\n\");\n    next = (ptr[len] == '\\t' ? &ptr[len + 1] : NULL);\n    switch(fields) {\n    case 0:\n      if(ptr[0]=='.') { /* skip preceding dots */\n        ptr++;\n        len--;\n      }\n      co->domain = Curl_memdup0(ptr, len);\n      if(!co->domain)\n        return CERR_OUT_OF_MEMORY;\n      break;\n    case 1:\n      /*\n       * flag: A TRUE/FALSE value indicating if all machines within a given\n       * domain can access the variable. Set TRUE when the cookie says\n       * .domain.com and to false when the domain is complete www.domain.com\n       */\n      co->tailmatch = !!strncasecompare(ptr, \"TRUE\", len);\n      break;\n    case 2:\n      /* The file format allows the path field to remain not filled in */\n      if(strncmp(\"TRUE\", ptr, len) && strncmp(\"FALSE\", ptr, len)) {\n        /* only if the path does not look like a boolean option! */\n        co->path = Curl_memdup0(ptr, len);\n        if(!co->path)\n          return CERR_OUT_OF_MEMORY;\n        else {\n          co->spath = sanitize_cookie_path(co->path);\n          if(!co->spath)\n            return CERR_OUT_OF_MEMORY;\n        }\n        break;\n      }\n      /* this does not look like a path, make one up! */\n      co->path = strdup(\"/\");\n      if(!co->path)\n        return CERR_OUT_OF_MEMORY;\n      co->spath = strdup(\"/\");\n      if(!co->spath)\n        return CERR_OUT_OF_MEMORY;\n      fields++; /* add a field and fall down to secure */\n      FALLTHROUGH();\n    case 3:\n      co->secure = FALSE;\n      if(strncasecompare(ptr, \"TRUE\", len)) {\n        if(secure || ci->running)\n          co->secure = TRUE;\n        else\n          return CERR_BAD_SECURE;\n      }\n      break;\n    case 4:\n      {\n        char *endp;\n        const char *p;\n        /* make sure curlx_strtoofft won't read past the current field */\n        for(p = ptr; p < &ptr[len] && ISDIGIT(*p); ++p)\n          ;\n        if(p == ptr || p != &ptr[len] ||\n           curlx_strtoofft(ptr, &endp, 10, &co->expires) || endp != &ptr[len])\n          return CERR_RANGE;\n      }\n      break;\n    case 5:\n      co->name = Curl_memdup0(ptr, len);\n      if(!co->name)\n        return CERR_OUT_OF_MEMORY;\n      else {\n        /* For Netscape file format cookies we check prefix on the name */\n        if(strncasecompare(\"__Secure-\", co->name, 9))\n          co->prefix_secure = TRUE;\n        else if(strncasecompare(\"__Host-\", co->name, 7))\n          co->prefix_host = TRUE;\n      }\n      break;\n    case 6:\n      co->value = Curl_memdup0(ptr, len);\n      if(!co->value)\n        return CERR_OUT_OF_MEMORY;\n      break;\n    }\n  }\n  if(6 == fields) {\n    /* we got a cookie with blank contents, fix it */\n    co->value = strdup(\"\");\n    if(!co->value)\n      return CERR_OUT_OF_MEMORY;\n    else\n      fields++;\n  }\n\n  if(7 != fields)\n    /* we did not find the sufficient number of fields */\n    return CERR_FIELDS;\n\n  return CERR_OK;\n}\n\nstatic int\nis_public_suffix(struct Curl_easy *data,\n                 struct Cookie *co,\n                 const char *domain)\n{\n#ifdef USE_LIBPSL\n  /*\n   * Check if the domain is a Public Suffix and if yes, ignore the cookie. We\n   * must also check that the data handle is not NULL since the psl code will\n   * dereference it.\n   */\n  DEBUGF(infof(data, \"PSL check set-cookie '%s' for domain=%s in %s\",\n         co->name, co->domain, domain));\n  if(data && (domain && co->domain && !Curl_host_is_ipnum(co->domain))) {\n    bool acceptable = FALSE;\n    char lcase[256];\n    char lcookie[256];\n    size_t dlen = strlen(domain);\n    size_t clen = strlen(co->domain);\n    if((dlen < sizeof(lcase)) && (clen < sizeof(lcookie))) {\n      const psl_ctx_t *psl = Curl_psl_use(data);\n      if(psl) {\n        /* the PSL check requires lowercase domain name and pattern */\n        Curl_strntolower(lcase, domain, dlen + 1);\n        Curl_strntolower(lcookie, co->domain, clen + 1);\n        acceptable = psl_is_cookie_domain_acceptable(psl, lcase, lcookie);\n        Curl_psl_release(data);\n      }\n      else\n        infof(data, \"libpsl problem, rejecting cookie for satety\");\n    }\n\n    if(!acceptable) {\n      infof(data, \"cookie '%s' dropped, domain '%s' must not \"\n            \"set cookies for '%s'\", co->name, domain, co->domain);\n      return CERR_PSL;\n    }\n  }\n#else\n  (void)data;\n  (void)co;\n  (void)domain;\n  DEBUGF(infof(data, \"NO PSL to check set-cookie '%s' for domain=%s in %s\",\n         co->name, co->domain, domain));\n#endif\n  return CERR_OK;\n}\n\nstatic int\nreplace_existing(struct Curl_easy *data,\n                 struct Cookie *co,\n                 struct CookieInfo *ci,\n                 bool secure,\n                 bool *replacep)\n{\n  bool replace_old = FALSE;\n  struct Curl_llist_node *replace_n = NULL;\n  struct Curl_llist_node *n;\n  size_t myhash = cookiehash(co->domain);\n  for(n = Curl_llist_head(&ci->cookielist[myhash]); n; n = Curl_node_next(n)) {\n    struct Cookie *clist = Curl_node_elem(n);\n    if(!strcmp(clist->name, co->name)) {\n      /* the names are identical */\n      bool matching_domains = FALSE;\n\n      if(clist->domain && co->domain) {\n        if(strcasecompare(clist->domain, co->domain))\n          /* The domains are identical */\n          matching_domains = TRUE;\n      }\n      else if(!clist->domain && !co->domain)\n        matching_domains = TRUE;\n\n      if(matching_domains && /* the domains were identical */\n         clist->spath && co->spath && /* both have paths */\n         clist->secure && !co->secure && !secure) {\n        size_t cllen;\n        const char *sep;\n\n        /*\n         * A non-secure cookie may not overlay an existing secure cookie.\n         * For an existing cookie \"a\" with path \"/login\", refuse a new\n         * cookie \"a\" with for example path \"/login/en\", while the path\n         * \"/loginhelper\" is ok.\n         */\n\n        sep = strchr(clist->spath + 1, '/');\n\n        if(sep)\n          cllen = sep - clist->spath;\n        else\n          cllen = strlen(clist->spath);\n\n        if(strncasecompare(clist->spath, co->spath, cllen)) {\n          infof(data, \"cookie '%s' for domain '%s' dropped, would \"\n                \"overlay an existing cookie\", co->name, co->domain);\n          return CERR_BAD_SECURE;\n        }\n      }\n    }\n\n    if(!replace_n && !strcmp(clist->name, co->name)) {\n      /* the names are identical */\n\n      if(clist->domain && co->domain) {\n        if(strcasecompare(clist->domain, co->domain) &&\n          (clist->tailmatch == co->tailmatch))\n          /* The domains are identical */\n          replace_old = TRUE;\n      }\n      else if(!clist->domain && !co->domain)\n        replace_old = TRUE;\n\n      if(replace_old) {\n        /* the domains were identical */\n\n        if(clist->spath && co->spath &&\n           !strcasecompare(clist->spath, co->spath))\n          replace_old = FALSE;\n        else if(!clist->spath != !co->spath)\n          replace_old = FALSE;\n      }\n\n      if(replace_old && !co->livecookie && clist->livecookie) {\n        /*\n         * Both cookies matched fine, except that the already present cookie\n         * is \"live\", which means it was set from a header, while the new one\n         * was read from a file and thus is not \"live\". \"live\" cookies are\n         * preferred so the new cookie is freed.\n         */\n        return CERR_LIVE_WINS;\n      }\n      if(replace_old)\n        replace_n = n;\n    }\n  }\n  if(replace_n) {\n    struct Cookie *repl = Curl_node_elem(replace_n);\n\n    /* when replacing, creationtime is kept from old */\n    co->creationtime = repl->creationtime;\n\n    /* unlink the old */\n    Curl_node_remove(replace_n);\n\n    /* free the old cookie */\n    freecookie(repl);\n  }\n  *replacep = replace_old;\n  return CERR_OK;\n}\n\n/*\n * Curl_cookie_add\n *\n * Add a single cookie line to the cookie keeping object. Be aware that\n * sometimes we get an IP-only hostname, and that might also be a numerical\n * IPv6 address.\n *\n * Returns NULL on out of memory or invalid cookie. This is suboptimal,\n * as they should be treated separately.\n */\nstruct Cookie *\nCurl_cookie_add(struct Curl_easy *data,\n                struct CookieInfo *ci,\n                bool httpheader, /* TRUE if HTTP header-style line */\n                bool noexpire, /* if TRUE, skip remove_expired() */\n                const char *lineptr,   /* first character of the line */\n                const char *domain, /* default domain */\n                const char *path,   /* full path used when this cookie is set,\n                                       used to get default path for the cookie\n                                       unless set */\n                bool secure)  /* TRUE if connection is over secure origin */\n{\n  struct Cookie *co;\n  size_t myhash;\n  int rc;\n  bool replaces = FALSE;\n\n  DEBUGASSERT(data);\n  DEBUGASSERT(MAX_SET_COOKIE_AMOUNT <= 255); /* counter is an unsigned char */\n  if(data->req.setcookies >= MAX_SET_COOKIE_AMOUNT)\n    return NULL;\n\n  /* First, alloc and init a new struct for it */\n  co = calloc(1, sizeof(struct Cookie));\n  if(!co)\n    return NULL; /* bail out if we are this low on memory */\n\n  if(httpheader)\n    rc = parse_cookie_header(data, co, ci, lineptr, domain, path, secure);\n  else\n    rc = parse_netscape(co, ci, lineptr, secure);\n\n  if(rc)\n    goto fail;\n\n  if(co->prefix_secure && !co->secure)\n    /* The __Secure- prefix only requires that the cookie be set secure */\n    goto fail;\n\n  if(co->prefix_host) {\n    /*\n     * The __Host- prefix requires the cookie to be secure, have a \"/\" path\n     * and not have a domain set.\n     */\n    if(co->secure && co->path && strcmp(co->path, \"/\") == 0 && !co->tailmatch)\n      ;\n    else\n      goto fail;\n  }\n\n  if(!ci->running &&    /* read from a file */\n     ci->newsession &&  /* clean session cookies */\n     !co->expires)      /* this is a session cookie since it does not expire */\n    goto fail;\n\n  co->livecookie = ci->running;\n  co->creationtime = ++ci->lastct;\n\n  /*\n   * Now we have parsed the incoming line, we must now check if this supersedes\n   * an already existing cookie, which it may if the previous have the same\n   * domain and path as this.\n   */\n\n  /* remove expired cookies */\n  if(!noexpire)\n    remove_expired(ci);\n\n  if(is_public_suffix(data, co, domain))\n    goto fail;\n\n  if(replace_existing(data, co, ci, secure, &replaces))\n    goto fail;\n\n  /* add this cookie to the list */\n  myhash = cookiehash(co->domain);\n  Curl_llist_append(&ci->cookielist[myhash], co, &co->node);\n\n  if(ci->running)\n    /* Only show this when NOT reading the cookies from a file */\n    infof(data, \"%s cookie %s=\\\"%s\\\" for domain %s, path %s, \"\n          \"expire %\" FMT_OFF_T,\n          replaces ? \"Replaced\":\"Added\", co->name, co->value,\n          co->domain, co->path, co->expires);\n\n  if(!replaces)\n    ci->numcookies++; /* one more cookie in the jar */\n\n  /*\n   * Now that we have added a new cookie to the jar, update the expiration\n   * tracker in case it is the next one to expire.\n   */\n  if(co->expires && (co->expires < ci->next_expiration))\n    ci->next_expiration = co->expires;\n\n  return co;\nfail:\n  freecookie(co);\n  return NULL;\n}\n\n\n/*\n * Curl_cookie_init()\n *\n * Inits a cookie struct to read data from a local file. This is always\n * called before any cookies are set. File may be NULL in which case only the\n * struct is initialized. Is file is \"-\" then STDIN is read.\n *\n * If 'newsession' is TRUE, discard all \"session cookies\" on read from file.\n *\n * Note that 'data' might be called as NULL pointer. If data is NULL, 'file'\n * will be ignored.\n *\n * Returns NULL on out of memory. Invalid cookies are ignored.\n */\nstruct CookieInfo *Curl_cookie_init(struct Curl_easy *data,\n                                    const char *file,\n                                    struct CookieInfo *ci,\n                                    bool newsession)\n{\n  FILE *handle = NULL;\n\n  if(!ci) {\n    int i;\n\n    /* we did not get a struct, create one */\n    ci = calloc(1, sizeof(struct CookieInfo));\n    if(!ci)\n      return NULL; /* failed to get memory */\n\n    /* This does not use the destructor callback since we want to add\n       and remove to lists while keeping the cookie struct intact */\n    for(i = 0; i < COOKIE_HASH_SIZE; i++)\n      Curl_llist_init(&ci->cookielist[i], NULL);\n    /*\n     * Initialize the next_expiration time to signal that we do not have enough\n     * information yet.\n     */\n    ci->next_expiration = CURL_OFF_T_MAX;\n  }\n  ci->newsession = newsession; /* new session? */\n\n  if(data) {\n    FILE *fp = NULL;\n    if(file && *file) {\n      if(!strcmp(file, \"-\"))\n        fp = stdin;\n      else {\n        fp = fopen(file, \"rb\");\n        if(!fp)\n          infof(data, \"WARNING: failed to open cookie file \\\"%s\\\"\", file);\n        else\n          handle = fp;\n      }\n    }\n\n    ci->running = FALSE; /* this is not running, this is init */\n    if(fp) {\n      struct dynbuf buf;\n      Curl_dyn_init(&buf, MAX_COOKIE_LINE);\n      while(Curl_get_line(&buf, fp)) {\n        char *lineptr = Curl_dyn_ptr(&buf);\n        bool headerline = FALSE;\n        if(checkprefix(\"Set-Cookie:\", lineptr)) {\n          /* This is a cookie line, get it! */\n          lineptr += 11;\n          headerline = TRUE;\n          while(*lineptr && ISBLANK(*lineptr))\n            lineptr++;\n        }\n\n        Curl_cookie_add(data, ci, headerline, TRUE, lineptr, NULL, NULL, TRUE);\n      }\n      Curl_dyn_free(&buf); /* free the line buffer */\n\n      /*\n       * Remove expired cookies from the hash. We must make sure to run this\n       * after reading the file, and not on every cookie.\n       */\n      remove_expired(ci);\n\n      if(handle)\n        fclose(handle);\n    }\n    data->state.cookie_engine = TRUE;\n  }\n  ci->running = TRUE;          /* now, we are running */\n\n  return ci;\n}\n\n/*\n * cookie_sort\n *\n * Helper function to sort cookies such that the longest path gets before the\n * shorter path. Path, domain and name lengths are considered in that order,\n * with the creationtime as the tiebreaker. The creationtime is guaranteed to\n * be unique per cookie, so we know we will get an ordering at that point.\n */\nstatic int cookie_sort(const void *p1, const void *p2)\n{\n  struct Cookie *c1 = *(struct Cookie **)p1;\n  struct Cookie *c2 = *(struct Cookie **)p2;\n  size_t l1, l2;\n\n  /* 1 - compare cookie path lengths */\n  l1 = c1->path ? strlen(c1->path) : 0;\n  l2 = c2->path ? strlen(c2->path) : 0;\n\n  if(l1 != l2)\n    return (l2 > l1) ? 1 : -1; /* avoid size_t <=> int conversions */\n\n  /* 2 - compare cookie domain lengths */\n  l1 = c1->domain ? strlen(c1->domain) : 0;\n  l2 = c2->domain ? strlen(c2->domain) : 0;\n\n  if(l1 != l2)\n    return (l2 > l1) ? 1 : -1; /* avoid size_t <=> int conversions */\n\n  /* 3 - compare cookie name lengths */\n  l1 = c1->name ? strlen(c1->name) : 0;\n  l2 = c2->name ? strlen(c2->name) : 0;\n\n  if(l1 != l2)\n    return (l2 > l1) ? 1 : -1;\n\n  /* 4 - compare cookie creation time */\n  return (c2->creationtime > c1->creationtime) ? 1 : -1;\n}\n\n/*\n * cookie_sort_ct\n *\n * Helper function to sort cookies according to creation time.\n */\nstatic int cookie_sort_ct(const void *p1, const void *p2)\n{\n  struct Cookie *c1 = *(struct Cookie **)p1;\n  struct Cookie *c2 = *(struct Cookie **)p2;\n\n  return (c2->creationtime > c1->creationtime) ? 1 : -1;\n}\n\n/*\n * Curl_cookie_getlist\n *\n * For a given host and path, return a linked list of cookies that the client\n * should send to the server if used now. The secure boolean informs the cookie\n * if a secure connection is achieved or not.\n *\n * It shall only return cookies that have not expired.\n *\n * Returns 0 when there is a list returned. Otherwise non-zero.\n */\nint Curl_cookie_getlist(struct Curl_easy *data,\n                        struct CookieInfo *ci,\n                        const char *host, const char *path,\n                        bool secure,\n                        struct Curl_llist *list)\n{\n  size_t matches = 0;\n  bool is_ip;\n  const size_t myhash = cookiehash(host);\n  struct Curl_llist_node *n;\n\n  Curl_llist_init(list, NULL);\n\n  if(!ci || !Curl_llist_count(&ci->cookielist[myhash]))\n    return 1; /* no cookie struct or no cookies in the struct */\n\n  /* at first, remove expired cookies */\n  remove_expired(ci);\n\n  /* check if host is an IP(v4|v6) address */\n  is_ip = Curl_host_is_ipnum(host);\n\n  for(n = Curl_llist_head(&ci->cookielist[myhash]);\n      n; n = Curl_node_next(n)) {\n    struct Cookie *co = Curl_node_elem(n);\n\n    /* if the cookie requires we are secure we must only continue if we are! */\n    if(co->secure ? secure : TRUE) {\n\n      /* now check if the domain is correct */\n      if(!co->domain ||\n         (co->tailmatch && !is_ip &&\n          cookie_tailmatch(co->domain, strlen(co->domain), host)) ||\n         ((!co->tailmatch || is_ip) && strcasecompare(host, co->domain)) ) {\n        /*\n         * the right part of the host matches the domain stuff in the\n         * cookie data\n         */\n\n        /*\n         * now check the left part of the path with the cookies path\n         * requirement\n         */\n        if(!co->spath || pathmatch(co->spath, path) ) {\n\n          /*\n           * This is a match and we add it to the return-linked-list\n           */\n          Curl_llist_append(list, co, &co->getnode);\n          matches++;\n          if(matches >= MAX_COOKIE_SEND_AMOUNT) {\n            infof(data, \"Included max number of cookies (%zu) in request!\",\n                  matches);\n            break;\n          }\n        }\n      }\n    }\n  }\n\n  if(matches) {\n    /*\n     * Now we need to make sure that if there is a name appearing more than\n     * once, the longest specified path version comes first. To make this\n     * the swiftest way, we just sort them all based on path length.\n     */\n    struct Cookie **array;\n    size_t i;\n\n    /* alloc an array and store all cookie pointers */\n    array = malloc(sizeof(struct Cookie *) * matches);\n    if(!array)\n      goto fail;\n\n    n = Curl_llist_head(list);\n\n    for(i = 0; n; n = Curl_node_next(n))\n      array[i++] = Curl_node_elem(n);\n\n    /* now sort the cookie pointers in path length order */\n    qsort(array, matches, sizeof(struct Cookie *), cookie_sort);\n\n    /* remake the linked list order according to the new order */\n    Curl_llist_destroy(list, NULL);\n\n    for(i = 0; i < matches; i++)\n      Curl_llist_append(list, array[i], &array[i]->getnode);\n\n    free(array); /* remove the temporary data again */\n  }\n\n  return 0; /* success */\n\nfail:\n  /* failure, clear up the allocated chain and return NULL */\n  Curl_llist_destroy(list, NULL);\n  return 2; /* error */\n}\n\n/*\n * Curl_cookie_clearall\n *\n * Clear all existing cookies and reset the counter.\n */\nvoid Curl_cookie_clearall(struct CookieInfo *ci)\n{\n  if(ci) {\n    unsigned int i;\n    for(i = 0; i < COOKIE_HASH_SIZE; i++) {\n      struct Curl_llist_node *n;\n      for(n = Curl_llist_head(&ci->cookielist[i]); n;) {\n        struct Cookie *c = Curl_node_elem(n);\n        struct Curl_llist_node *e = Curl_node_next(n);\n        Curl_node_remove(n);\n        freecookie(c);\n        n = e;\n      }\n    }\n    ci->numcookies = 0;\n  }\n}\n\n/*\n * Curl_cookie_clearsess\n *\n * Free all session cookies in the cookies list.\n */\nvoid Curl_cookie_clearsess(struct CookieInfo *ci)\n{\n  unsigned int i;\n\n  if(!ci)\n    return;\n\n  for(i = 0; i < COOKIE_HASH_SIZE; i++) {\n    struct Curl_llist_node *n = Curl_llist_head(&ci->cookielist[i]);\n    struct Curl_llist_node *e = NULL;\n\n    for(; n; n = e) {\n      struct Cookie *curr = Curl_node_elem(n);\n      e = Curl_node_next(n); /* in case the node is removed, get it early */\n      if(!curr->expires) {\n        Curl_node_remove(n);\n        freecookie(curr);\n        ci->numcookies--;\n      }\n    }\n  }\n}\n\n/*\n * Curl_cookie_cleanup()\n *\n * Free a \"cookie object\" previous created with Curl_cookie_init().\n */\nvoid Curl_cookie_cleanup(struct CookieInfo *ci)\n{\n  if(ci) {\n    Curl_cookie_clearall(ci);\n    free(ci); /* free the base struct as well */\n  }\n}\n\n/*\n * get_netscape_format()\n *\n * Formats a string for Netscape output file, w/o a newline at the end.\n * Function returns a char * to a formatted line. The caller is responsible\n * for freeing the returned pointer.\n */\nstatic char *get_netscape_format(const struct Cookie *co)\n{\n  return aprintf(\n    \"%s\"     /* httponly preamble */\n    \"%s%s\\t\" /* domain */\n    \"%s\\t\"   /* tailmatch */\n    \"%s\\t\"   /* path */\n    \"%s\\t\"   /* secure */\n    \"%\" FMT_OFF_T \"\\t\"   /* expires */\n    \"%s\\t\"   /* name */\n    \"%s\",    /* value */\n    co->httponly ? \"#HttpOnly_\" : \"\",\n    /*\n     * Make sure all domains are prefixed with a dot if they allow\n     * tailmatching. This is Mozilla-style.\n     */\n    (co->tailmatch && co->domain && co->domain[0] != '.') ? \".\" : \"\",\n    co->domain ? co->domain : \"unknown\",\n    co->tailmatch ? \"TRUE\" : \"FALSE\",\n    co->path ? co->path : \"/\",\n    co->secure ? \"TRUE\" : \"FALSE\",\n    co->expires,\n    co->name,\n    co->value ? co->value : \"\");\n}\n\n/*\n * cookie_output()\n *\n * Writes all internally known cookies to the specified file. Specify\n * \"-\" as filename to write to stdout.\n *\n * The function returns non-zero on write failure.\n */\nstatic CURLcode cookie_output(struct Curl_easy *data,\n                              struct CookieInfo *ci,\n                              const char *filename)\n{\n  FILE *out = NULL;\n  bool use_stdout = FALSE;\n  char *tempstore = NULL;\n  CURLcode error = CURLE_OK;\n\n  if(!ci)\n    /* no cookie engine alive */\n    return CURLE_OK;\n\n  /* at first, remove expired cookies */\n  remove_expired(ci);\n\n  if(!strcmp(\"-\", filename)) {\n    /* use stdout */\n    out = stdout;\n    use_stdout = TRUE;\n  }\n  else {\n    error = Curl_fopen(data, filename, &out, &tempstore);\n    if(error)\n      goto error;\n  }\n\n  fputs(\"# Netscape HTTP Cookie File\\n\"\n        \"# https://curl.se/docs/http-cookies.html\\n\"\n        \"# This file was generated by libcurl! Edit at your own risk.\\n\\n\",\n        out);\n\n  if(ci->numcookies) {\n    unsigned int i;\n    size_t nvalid = 0;\n    struct Cookie **array;\n    struct Curl_llist_node *n;\n\n    array = calloc(1, sizeof(struct Cookie *) * ci->numcookies);\n    if(!array) {\n      error = CURLE_OUT_OF_MEMORY;\n      goto error;\n    }\n\n    /* only sort the cookies with a domain property */\n    for(i = 0; i < COOKIE_HASH_SIZE; i++) {\n      for(n = Curl_llist_head(&ci->cookielist[i]); n;\n          n = Curl_node_next(n)) {\n        struct Cookie *co = Curl_node_elem(n);\n        if(!co->domain)\n          continue;\n        array[nvalid++] = co;\n      }\n    }\n\n    qsort(array, nvalid, sizeof(struct Cookie *), cookie_sort_ct);\n\n    for(i = 0; i < nvalid; i++) {\n      char *format_ptr = get_netscape_format(array[i]);\n      if(!format_ptr) {\n        free(array);\n        error = CURLE_OUT_OF_MEMORY;\n        goto error;\n      }\n      fprintf(out, \"%s\\n\", format_ptr);\n      free(format_ptr);\n    }\n\n    free(array);\n  }\n\n  if(!use_stdout) {\n    fclose(out);\n    out = NULL;\n    if(tempstore && Curl_rename(tempstore, filename)) {\n      unlink(tempstore);\n      error = CURLE_WRITE_ERROR;\n      goto error;\n    }\n  }\n\n  /*\n   * If we reach here we have successfully written a cookie file so there is\n   * no need to inspect the error, any error case should have jumped into the\n   * error block below.\n   */\n  free(tempstore);\n  return CURLE_OK;\n\nerror:\n  if(out && !use_stdout)\n    fclose(out);\n  free(tempstore);\n  return error;\n}\n\nstatic struct curl_slist *cookie_list(struct Curl_easy *data)\n{\n  struct curl_slist *list = NULL;\n  struct curl_slist *beg;\n  unsigned int i;\n  struct Curl_llist_node *n;\n\n  if(!data->cookies || (data->cookies->numcookies == 0))\n    return NULL;\n\n  for(i = 0; Now I can see all the defects clearly. The removed check was:\n```c\n#if SIZEOF_SIZE_T == 4\n  if(insize > UINT_MAX/4)\n    return CURLE_OUT_OF_MEMORY;\n#endif\n```\n\nThis check is important on 32-bit systems. The allocation size is `(insize + 2) / 3 * 4 + 1`. Let me trace through why this check is needed:- insize in bytes  \n- (insize + 2) / 3: quantums (groups of 3 bytes in base64)\n- ((insize + 2) / 3 * 4): total size needed (each quantum becomes 4 bytes)- ((insize + 2) / 3 * 4 + 1): +1 for null terminator\n\nIf insize = UINT_MAX/4 + 1:\n- (insize + 2) / 3 = (UINT_MAX/4 + 3) / 3 ≈ UINT_MAX/12\n- (insize + 2) / 3 * 4 ≈ UINT_MAX/3\n\nBut if insize = UINT_MAX - 2:\n- (insize + 2) / 3 = UINT_MAX / 3\n- (insize + 2) / 3 * 4 could overflow!\n\nActually, on a 32-bit system:\n- UINT_MAX = 4294967295\n- If insize = 1073741823 (which is UINT_MAX/4):  \n  - (insize + 2) / 3 ≈ 357913941\n  - 357913941 * 4 = 1431655764 (fits in 32 bits)\n- If insize = 1073741824 (UINT_MAX/4 + 1):\n  - (insize + 2) / 3 ≈ 357913942\n  - 357913942 * 4 = 1431655768 (still fits)\n\nThe real danger emerges when the intermediate multiplication wraps around to a small value.
